{"text":"\n    \n\n    \n    \n    \n        \n            \n            \n            \n            \n                Development Tools\n            \n        \n    \n    \n\n    \n        \n        \n        \n    \n        \n        \n            Learn how Headroom compresses AI agent context for Claude Code, Codex, Cursor, MCP servers, proxy mode, logs, tool output, and RAG snippets to reduce token use.\n        \n        \n    \n\n    \n    \n    \n    \n    \n    \n\n    \n        \n    \n\n\n\n\n\n    \n    \n    \n    chopratejas/headroom is a tool for context compression for AI Agents. The problem it solves is very realistic: while the agent is running commands, reading logs, searching for code, and stuffing RAG fragments, the context window will soon be filled, and the cost and delay will rise together.\nThe idea behind Headroom is to compress tool output, logs, files, RAG clips and session history before the content enters LLM. The goal written in the README is very straightforward: reduce 60-95% tokens while trying to maintain the quality of answers.\nWhat problem does it solve?\nMany agent tools now do not have models that are not smart enough, but the context is too dirty:\n\ngrep, rg, log query returns hundreds or thousands of rows at a time;\nRAG search fragments are repeated, redundant, and formatted;\nThere are a large number of low-value fields in JSON, stack trace, and SQL results;\nAfter multiple rounds of debugging, the old output occupies the context;\nTools such as Claude Code, Codex, Cursor, and Aider each maintain context, making it difficult to share memory.\n\nHeadroom is the “cleaner before entering the model”. It does not replace LLM, nor does it replace RAG, but adds a layer of compression, routing, caching, and traceable retrieval in front of LLM.\nCore Competencies\nFrom the README, Headroom has several main usage forms:\n\nLibrary: directly call compress(messages) in Python or TypeScript;\nProxy: Use headroom proxy --port 8787 as OpenAI-compatible proxy;\nAgent wrap: Use headroom wrap claude|codex|cursor|aider|copilot to wrap an existing Agent;\nMCP Server: Provides headroom_compress, headroom_retrieve, headroom_stats for use by MCP clients;\nCross-agent memory: Let Claude, Codex, Gemini and other tools share local memory and automatically remove duplicates;\nheadroom learn: dig experience from failed sessions, write CLAUDE.md or AGENTS.md;\nReversible compression: The original text will not be deleted and can be retrieved through the search tool if needed.\n\nThese forms are crucial. It is not an SDK that can only be embedded in the code, nor can it only be used as a proxy. You can start with the lightest wrap mode and decide whether to integrate it into your own application.\nHow does it compress?\nThere are several keywords in the structure of Headroom:\n\nContentRouter: identify the content type and select the corresponding compressor;\nSmartCrusher: prefers to process structured content such as JSON;\nCodeCompressor: prefers processing code and AST;\nKompress-base: used for text compression;\nCacheAligner: Make the prompt prefix more stable and improve the provider’s KV cache hit rate;\nCCR: Save the original text and retrieve it through retrieve when needed.\n\nIn human terms, it does not roughly summarize all the content into a paragraph, but first determines the content type and then selects different compression strategies. Code, JSON, plain text, logs and RAG fragments should not be compressed in the same way.\nQuick installation\nThe installation method given in the README is very straightforward:\n\n\n1\n2\n\n\npip install \"headroom-ai[all]\"\nnpm install headroom-ai\n\nThe Python side requires Python 3.10+. After installation, you can try these commands first:\n\n\n1\n2\n3\n\n\nheadroom wrap claude\nheadroom proxy --port 8787\nheadroom perf\n\nIf you are using the MCP client, you can go:\n\n\n1\n\n\nheadroom mcp install\n\nIf you just want to verify the effect, the easiest thing is to run headroom perf first to see how many tokens it can save for typical workloads. After confirming that it is available, connect it to Claude Code, Codex, Cursor or your own OpenAI-compatible client.\nWhat is the difference between ## and ordinary summary?\nThe biggest problem with ordinary abstracts is that they are irreversible. The log is summarized as “Database connection failed”, and you can’t see the original error code, timestamp, call stack and context. If the Agent needs details later, he can only check again.\nOne of the key points of Headroom is reversible: the original content is saved locally, compressed and passed to the model; if the model requires the original text, it is retrieved through headroom_retrieve. This design is more suitable for debugging, code search, and production log analysis, because these scenarios often require going back to details.\nOf course, this also means you have to manage local storage and privacy boundaries. Although the README emphasizes local-first, as long as you send the compressed content to the cloud model, you still have to handle it according to your own data security requirements.\nWhich scenarios are suitable?\nI think Headroom is best suited for these scenarios:\n\nClaude Code, Codex, and Cursor often slow down because the tool output is too long;\nUse Agent to analyze large warehouses, search results and file fragments can easily explode the context;\nWhen troubleshooting, SRE should show logs, traces, configurations and command output to the model;\nWhen doing RAG applications, the search results are seriously redundant;\nWant to share local memory between multiple Agent tools;\nWant to integrate MCP tools into existing AI workflows.\n\nIf you only ask for a few chats occasionally, or the prompt is very short, you don’t necessarily need it. The value of Headroom mainly appears when “Agent is really doing work”.\nWhat should you pay attention to when using it?\nContextual compression is not magic. It can save tokens, but it may also bring new problems:\n\nWhen the compression strategy is inappropriate, the model may not be able to obtain key details;\nCode and log scenarios need to test whether retrieve is reliable;\nWhen accepting the proxy mode, confirm which local and cloud links the request passes through;\nWhen used by teams, local caching, session recording and sensitive data retention policies must be defined;\nDon’t just look at token savings, but also look at task completion rate and misjudgment rate.\n\nMy suggestion is to test with real tasks instead of just watching demos. For example, take a set of historical bugs, CI logs, RAG queries and code search tasks, and compare the cost, speed and answer quality of “feeding the model directly” and “passing through Headroom” respectively.\nSummary\nHeadroom is a typical “contextual engineering” tool. It does not seek to recreate an Agent, but stands between the Agent and the LLM, cleaning and shortening the content that enters the model, while retaining the ability to retrieve the original text.\nIt’s suitable for people who are already using Claude Code, Codex, Cursor, Aider, Copilot CLI or MCP tools. If your pain point is “the model context is often overwhelmed by logs and tool output”, Headroom is worth trying; if your problem is just insufficient model capabilities, simply compressing the context may not necessarily solve it.\nReference sources\n\nchopratejas/headroom - GitHub\n\nFAQ\nWhat is this project?\nIt is an AI tooling project covered in this article, with a focus on what it does, how to use it, and when it is worth trying.\nWho is it for?\nIt is mainly for developers and AI tool users who want a practical way to connect the project to real workflows rather than only read the README.\nWhat should I check before using it?\nCheck installation method, supported tools, data and permission boundaries, and whether the project is still changing quickly.\nIs it suitable for production use?\nTreat it as a tool to test carefully first. Verify behavior on a small workflow before applying it to sensitive or production tasks.\n\n\n\n\n    \n\n\n    \n","url":"https://knightli.com/en/2026/06/06/headroom-ai-context-compression/"}
{"text":"Token Optimization Guide for GitHub Copilot\nImportantThis is not official GitHub or Microsoft guidance. This guide is a community resource born from real-world field experience — patterns observed, techniques tested, and lessons learned by practitioners adopting AI for development purposes. It reflects industry backspark: practical knowledge gathered from the ground up, not top-down product documentation. Use it to inform about optimization strategies, and adapt what works for the context of your customer. Official guidance lives at docs.github.com/copilot.\n\n\nA practical, data-driven guide to reducing token consumption while maintaining code quality.\nCovers Chat, Inline, and Coding Agent workflows.\n\n\nQuick Start — 12 Things to Do Right Now\n\nJune 1, 2026 — Usage-Based Billing (UBB) is live. GitHub Copilot now bills real tokens (input + output + cached) drawn from pooled AI credits ($30/seat Business, $70/seat Enterprise) instead of request counters. Every technique in this guide translates directly into credit savings — and cache-friendly habits matter more than ever. See Enterprise Governance for customer guardrails and Model Selection & Pricing for model-cost guidance.\n\n\nOutput tokens cost much more than input tokens. That's the most important pricing fact in this guide. Anthropic's public pricing makes the asymmetry concrete ($1/$5 Haiku, $3/$15 Sonnet, $5/$25 Opus per MTok input/output). Copilot's exact per-model UBB pricing table is not public yet, but UBB still makes verbose output disproportionately expensive. Most input tokens come from file context, history, and tool schemas — not from what you type. Your typed prompt is a tiny fraction of total input. Start with output control, then tackle structural input wins.\n\nDon't have time to read the full guide? Do these today and cut your token usage:\n\n\n\n#\nAction\nPrimary Effect\nTime to Set Up\n\n\n\n\n1\nRequest code-only responses — add Code only, no explanation. to copilot-instructions.md. Highest per-token ROI: output costs 5× more than input, and this cuts 40-70% of output on every code task, permanently\nShrinks response length\n0 minutes\n\n\n2\nConstrain output format by default — add Bullets over paragraphs. No explanations unless asked. to copilot-instructions.md\nKeeps answers terse\n0 minutes\n\n\n3\nShrink your always-on context — compress copilot-instructions.md AND prune AGENTS.md to landmines only. Every token in either file is billed on every interaction (and every agent step). Strip filler, delete anything the agent discovers by reading code, delete LLM-generated /init boilerplate\nReduces always-on input/context\n15 minutes\n\n\n4\nDefault to Auto model selection + protect cache stability — use Auto as the baseline because it chooses from the supported Auto pool and gives a paid-plan discount. In long expensive threads, keep {model, active MCP set, active agent/profile} stable. If you must switch lanes, start a fresh chat with a short handoff summary. See Model Selection & Pricing\nLowers billed rate on eligible usage and preserves cached-input discounts\n0 minutes\n\n\n5\nUse Ask Mode for simple questions — reserve Agent Mode for multi-step tasks\nAvoids agent overhead\n0 minutes (just choose the right mode)\n\n\n6\nScope context with applyTo: paths — split one large instructions file into small scoped ones that load only when relevant\nReduces always-on input/context\n15 minutes\n\n\n7\nBe precise in your prompts — \"Add null check to getUser()\" not \"Can you please look at this and maybe add some error handling?\" Note: your typed prompt is a small fraction of total input; precision matters more for quality than for raw token savings\nImproves task targeting\n0 minutes\n\n\n8\nRetune prompts to the target model — provider prompting guides change by model/version. Paste the official guide URL into Copilot and ask it to adapt .github/copilot-instructions.md, agent profiles, or app prompts for the model you actually use\nReduces rework\n10 minutes per model change\n\n\n9\nAudit your MCP servers and injected tools — disable unused MCP servers and VS Code extensions that add skills/tools; use a clean coding profile or focused custom agent for repeat workflows. Each MCP tool costs ~100-500 tokens per agent step\nRemoves tool/schema overhead\n5-10 minutes\n\n\n10\nConvert rich files to Markdown before AI work — .docx, .pdf, .pptx, .xlsx, HTML, images, audio, video, and ZIPs carry format tax. Marc Bara's writeup shows the cost; use Microsoft MarkItDown before chat, agent, or RAG ingestion\nReduces noisy input context\n5 minutes\n\n\n11\nRun /chronicle cost tips and /chronicle improve weekly (Copilot CLI only, experimental) — these slash commands work in interactive Copilot CLI sessions (not VS Code), not as a general Copilot Chat feature. cost tips analyzes your token spend and suggests reductions; improve finds recurring confusion in your CLI session history and generates custom-instruction fixes so the same misread intent stops costing tokens forever\nCuts recurring rework and direct token spend\n2 minutes per run\n\n\n12\nTry CodeAct for long tool chains (Copilot CLI only, optional external plugin) — copilot-codeact-plugin collapses multi-step tool chains into one sandboxed execution, which can reduce repeated replay of system prompt, prior messages, and tool definitions\nReduces tool-loop replay\n10-15 minutes\n\n\n13\nPlan first, then execute in a fresh session — use plan mode (CLI) or Ask mode (VS Code) to agree the approach with a strong model, save the plan to plan.md or an issue, then run the execution from that plan in a clean session — often with a cheaper model. Reaching the right outcome the first time avoids the expensive rework of an agent coding in the wrong direction. See Plan First, Then Execute §2.5.9\nAvoids wrong-direction rework; cheaper execution lane\n0 minutes (just sequence the work)\n\n\n\nLooking at this from an enterprise or customer-governance angle instead of an individual setup angle? Start with Enterprise Governance. That chapter covers AI-credit budgets, per-user tightening, model-access policy, org instructions, and separate-organization tradeoffs.\nFigures above are scoped to the mechanism named in each row, are not additive, and do not equal total bill reduction.\nOutput control (#1, #2) pays off immediately and compounds — set it once, save on every call. Structural input control (#3, #6) compounds across every interaction. Model routing (#4, #5) reduces cost at the billing tier. Model-specific prompt tuning (#8) cuts waste by improving first-pass quality. MCP audit (#9) eliminates thousands of hidden tokens per agent task. Markdown conversion (#10) removes DOCX/PDF/HTML layout noise before the model ever sees it.\n\nGuide Contents\nPart 1: Why Tokens Matter\nUnderstand BPE tokenization, why tokens matter for cost/speed/limits, and how GitHub Copilot uses tokens behind the scenes.\n→ Read Part 1\n\nPart 2: The Techniques\n2.1 Prompt Compression\nCaveman-speak, intensity levels (lite/full/ultra), structured formats, abbreviations, and code-centric prompting. 30-50% input token savings; combine with output control (2.4) for output savings.\n2.2 Language Comparison\nData-backed comparison: English is the most token-efficient language in these examples. CJK costs 1.7-2.4x more. Includes tokenization tables for 8 languages.\n2.3 Context Management\nCompress system instructions, compress memory files, scope context with applyTo, close unused editor tabs, convert non-text files to Markdown before AI work, configure Content Exclusion (Business/Enterprise admins), start fresh conversations. Control what gets sent to the model.\n2.4 Output Control\n\"Code only, no explanation.\" Constrain response format. Set terse output as project default.\n2.5 Workflow Optimization\nTerse commit messages, one-line PR reviews, Ask vs Agent mode selection, model-specific prompt tuning, and when NOT to compress.\n2.6 The Always-On Context Problem\nResearch on LLM-generated context files suggests they often hurt agent correctness while inflating token cost. The same lesson applies to both AGENTS.md and .github/copilot-instructions.md — they are distinct conventions (different filenames, different historical owners) that nonetheless function as always-on context for Copilot today. Apply the \"landmines only\" approach to whichever file(s) your repo uses. Treat context files like a bug tracker, not a wiki.\n2.7 MCP & Tool Costs\nThe hidden token tax: each MCP tool costs 100-500 tokens per agent step. 15 servers × 15 steps = 265K tokens of overhead. Audit guide included.\n\nPart 3: Comparisons & Data\nHead-to-head prompt comparisons, language tokenization tables, the complete technique-by-technique matrix (40+ techniques), and quality impact assessment with the diminishing returns curve.\n→ Read Part 3\n\nPart 4: Practical Setup\nStep-by-step: configure Copilot, optimize the Coding Agent, configure agent mode, and build the habit. Includes VS Code settings, decision frameworks, and a 4-week adoption plan.\n→ Read Part 4\n\nPart 4.2: Model Selection & Pricing\nDedicated page on models, PRU-era multiplier history, current Auto guidance, plan availability, and where vendor input/output token pricing fits while Copilot's exact per-model UBB table remains unpublished. Includes links to the official GitHub Docs pages for Auto model selection, billing, and plan/model availability.\n→ Read Part 4.2\n\nPart 4.3: Enterprise Governance\nDedicated chapter for customer-facing admin guidance: usage-based billing guardrails, AI-credit budgets, spend cohorts, FinOps-as-code automation, model-access policy, org-level instructions, and separate-organization tradeoffs.\n→ Read Part 4.3\n\nNeed the glossary, quick terms, tools, or core external links? Go to Guide Home.\n\nHighest-Impact Techniques\nRanked by cost impact. Output first — it costs 5× more per token than input.\n\nOutput control — \"Code only, no explanation\" + terse default in copilot-instructions.md. 40-70% output savings on code tasks, 30-60% across all interactions. One instruction, permanent.\nShrink always-on context (copilot-instructions.md + AGENTS.md) — compress filler, prune to landmines only, delete LLM-generated boilerplate. Compounds on every interaction and agent step; 20-23% agent-task reduction plus better correctness\nAsk Mode for simple questions — 60-90% savings by avoiding Agent overhead\nAudit MCP servers and injected tools — disable unused servers/extensions, or use a clean coding profile/custom agent, to save 5K-190K tokens per agent task\nAuto model selection — lower-cost default routing plus paid-plan discount on eligible usage, zero effort\nConvert rich files to Markdown first — avoid paying for Word/PDF/HTML layout noise in chat, agent, and RAG workflows\nRetune prompts to the target model — better first-pass output reduces repeated clarification turns\nPrecise prompts — 20-40% of user-prompt input tokens; more important for quality than raw savings\n\n\nThis is a living document. As tokenizer technology evolves, model capabilities change, and new techniques emerge, this guide will be updated. Check the repository for the latest version.\n","url":"https://github.com/olivomarco/github-copilot-token-optimization"}
{"text":"Awesome LLM Token Optimization \n\nA curated list of strategies, tools, papers, and resources for reducing LLM token costs and improving efficiency in production.\n\nBuilding with LLMs is expensive. An agent processing 10 reasoning steps can consume 50K-100K tokens per task. This list collects everything you need to cut costs by 80-99% without sacrificing quality.\nContents\n\nQuick Wins\nPrompt Caching\nBatch APIs\nModel Routing\nPrompt Compression\nContext Window Management\nKV Cache Optimization\nBrowser Tool Efficiency\nCost Tracking Tools\nPricing Comparison\nPrompt Engineering for Efficiency\nComprehensive Guides\nAcademic Papers\nCommunity Resources\n\n\nQuick Wins\nThe highest-impact strategies ranked by effort-to-savings ratio:\n\n\n\nStrategy\nSavings\nEffort\nLink\n\n\n\n\nPrompt caching\n90% input tokens\nAdd cache headers\nPrompt Caching\n\n\nToken-efficient tool use\n70% output reduction\nFlip a flag\nPrompt Engineering\n\n\nBatch API\n50%\nQueue non-urgent work\nBatch APIs\n\n\nModel routing\n60-95%\nRoute by task complexity\nModel Routing\n\n\nResponse caching\n100% on repeats\nAdd a cache layer\nComprehensive Guides\n\n\nPrompt compression\n5-20x\nUse LLMLingua\nPrompt Compression\n\n\n\nCombined pipeline: Cache prefix (90%) + route to cheapest model (60-95%) + batch non-urgent (50%) + compress prompts (5-20x) + cache responses (100% on repeats) = 95-99% cost reduction vs. naive approach.\nPrompt Caching\nReuse previously-processed prompt prefixes to avoid re-computing the same tokens.\nProvider Docs\n\nAnthropic Prompt Caching - 90% discount, 5min/1hr TTL. Minimum cacheable prefix: 4,096 tokens on Opus 4.6/Haiku 4.5, 1,024 on Sonnet 4.6/Opus 4.8/Sonnet 5.\nAnthropic Caching Announcement - Blog post explaining economics.\nAnthropic Token-Saving Updates - Cache-aware rate limits, simplified caching.\nAnthropic Extended Thinking + Caching - Thinking blocks get cached in tool-use loops.\nOpenAI Prompt Caching - 50% discount, automatic for 1024+ token prompts. Extended cache retention now defaults to 24h on the GPT-5 series (mandatory on GPT-5.5+), keeping prefixes warm far longer.\nOpenAI Prompt Caching Cookbook - Advanced techniques with code.\nGoogle Gemini Context Caching - Implicit (auto) and explicit caching, 90% discount.\nGoogle Vertex AI Caching - Enterprise context caching.\nDeepSeek KV Cache - Disk-based, 64-token granularity. V4 Flash cache hits: $0.0028/M vs $0.14/M base (98% savings). Migration: deepseek-chat and deepseek-reasoner aliases retire July 24, 2026 — update to deepseek-v4-flash or deepseek-v4-pro.\nDeepSeek Context Caching on Disk - Announcement of disk-based context caching cutting input cost ~10x on cache hits.\n\nStrategy: Cached Prefix Pattern\nStructure prompts so the system prompt + user profile is the first ~2,000 tokens. All subsequent calls share this prefix. For bulk operations (e.g., scoring 50 items): 1x full + 49x at 10% = 88% total savings.\nTools\n\nautocache - Transparent Anthropic proxy that auto-injects cache_control breakpoints at optimal positions; up to 90% cost and 85% latency reduction. \n\nBatch APIs\n50% discounts for non-time-critical requests. Combine with caching for 95% savings.\n\nAnthropic Message Batches - Up to 10,000 requests, 24hr turnaround.\nAnthropic Batches Announcement - Use cases and GA details.\nOpenAI Batch API - 50% discount, 50K requests per file.\nOpenAI Batch API FAQ - Limits and behavior.\nGoogle Gemini Batch API - 50% discount, combinable with context caching.\nGoogle Vertex Batch Prediction - Enterprise batch.\nCurator - Batch-inference and synthetic-data library; batch=True gives ~50% savings across OpenAI/Anthropic/Gemini/Mistral with built-in caching and retries. \n\nModel Routing\nRoute simple tasks to cheaper models. 80% of typical LLM calls don't need the most expensive model.\nFrameworks\n\nRouteLLM - Open-source LLM router by LMSYS. Trains routers from preference data; 2x+ cost reduction. Note: last commit Aug 2024; LMSYS team shifted focus to Chatbot Arena. \nLiteLLM - SDK + proxy for 100+ LLMs with routing, cost tracking. Strategies: least-busy, cost-based, latency-based. \nNotDiamond - Per-query best-model selection. Note: the Python SDK was archived Dec 2025 (read-only); the notdiamond.ai service remains active. \nBifrost - 50x faster than LiteLLM; adaptive load balancer, 1000+ models. \nvLLM Semantic Router - System-level signal-driven router for Mixture-of-Models across cloud, data center, and edge. v0.3 \"Themis\" (June 2026); SAAR adds session-aware model selection cutting model switches 79% in multi-agent deployments. \nLLMRouter - Open-source routing library with 16+ routers (single-round, multi-turn, agentic, personalized) and a unified CLI. \nPortkey AI Gateway - Open-source AI gateway routing to 1,600+ LLMs with guardrails, caching, and load balancing. Acquired by Palo Alto Networks (May 2026); gateway remains open-source under Apache 2.0. \nOpenRouter - Unified API for 300+ models with auto-router.\nMartian Router - Patent-pending; cuts costs 20-97% via \"Model Mapping\".\n\nCurated Lists\n\nAwesome AI Model Routing - Comprehensive list of routing approaches.\n\nResearch\n\nRouteLLM paper - LMSYS blog on cost-quality tradeoffs.\nIBM LLM Routers - IBM's research on training routers.\nvLLM Session-Aware Agentic Routing (SAAR) - Router-owned session memory with hard locks around tool loops cuts model switches 79% and estimated cost 78.7% in multi-agent deployments.\nLLM Routing Explained - Intuitive guide.\nvLLM Semantic Router paper - Signal-driven decision routing for Mixture-of-Modality models; composable signal orchestration across heuristic and neural classifiers.\n\nPrompt Compression\nReduce prompt size while preserving information quality.\nTools\n\nLLMLingua - Up to 20x compression. Coarse-to-fine iterative method. Integrates with LangChain/LlamaIndex. \nHeadroom - Compress tool outputs, logs, files, and RAG chunks before they reach the LLM (60-95% fewer tokens); library, proxy, and MCP server. Claude Code/Cursor/Aider compatible.\ncode2prompt - Codebase to LLM prompt with token counting. \nRTK - Single-binary Rust CLI proxy that compresses dev-command output 60-90% before it reaches a coding agent's context. Works with Claude Code, Cursor, Copilot, Gemini CLI. \nTOON - Token-Oriented Object Notation: a compact, schema-aware encoding for passing JSON-like data to LLMs; 30-60% fewer tokens than JSON on uniform arrays of objects. \nllmtrim - Quality-gated local proxy and MCP server that compresses prompts, tool outputs, and replies before they reach the LLM, reverting any step that doesn't save tokens (project-reported -31% input / -74% output across 112 A/B cases). Rust CLI plus multi-language library bindings and a WebAssembly/JS package. \nlean-ctx - Rust binary context intelligence layer for AI coding agents; 60-90% fewer tokens via shell-output compression and 10 cached-read modes; MCP server with 76 tools and cross-session memory. Works with Claude Code, Cursor, Copilot, Windsurf, Gemini CLI, and 30+ others. \n\nResearch\n\nCompactPrompt - Unified prompt + data compression pipeline.\nEfficient Prompting Survey - Survey of efficient prompting methods.\n\nThe full prompt-compression paper table lives in the Academic Papers section below.\nGuides\n\nLLMLingua Research Blog - Microsoft Research deep dive.\nPrompt Compression Tutorial (FreeCodeCamp) - Practical guide with code.\nPrompt Compression Overview (MLM) - 6x to 480x compression ratios.\nAwesome LLM Compression - Curated paper list.\n\nLossless Compression Principles\nRule-based lossless distillation achieves 3-4:1 compression without any model:\nStrip prose transitions, hedging, rhetoric, and common knowledge. Preserve numbers, entities, decisions, constraints, and risks. Transform prose into dense bullets and verbose text into semicolon-joined clauses. Split into 3,000-5,000 token self-contained sections that load independently.\nContext Window Management\nKey Research\n\nContext Rot toolkit (Chroma) - Toolkit reproducing how LLMs degrade well before context limits (18 models tested).\nRAG vs Long Context (Elastic) - RAG is 1250x cheaper for many queries.\nLong Context RAG (Databricks) - Degradation after 32K-64K tokens.\nContext Extension Survey - All context extension techniques surveyed.\n\nProvider Docs\n\nAnthropic Long Context Tips - Place docs at top, use XML tags.\nAnthropic Context Windows - How context works, server-side compaction.\nAnthropic Context Engineering - Finding the smallest high-signal token set.\nAnthropic Long-Running Agents - Managing context across extended workflows.\n\nChunking & Splitting\n\nPinecone Chunking Guide - Fixed-length, semantic, hierarchical.\nAdvanced Chunking (Galileo) - Agentic and LLM-based.\nContext Engineering Guide - Curated papers and tools.\nEfficient Context Management (JetBrains) - Observation masking vs summarization.\nOpenProvence - Open reranker-pruner that drops ~99% off-topic sentences and compresses 80-90% of relevant RAG text; CPU-friendly. \n\nKV Cache Optimization\nServer-side optimizations for inference efficiency.\nInference Engines\n\nCompression Tools\n\nResearch\n\nSpeculative Sampling - Fast inference via speculative decoding.\nAwesome KV Cache Compression - Must-read paper list.\n\nThe full KV-cache paper table lives in the Academic Papers section below.\nEducational\n\nmini-sglang - Learn LLM serving internals.\ntiny-llm - Build a tiny vLLM on Apple Silicon.\n\nBrowser Tool Efficiency\nDifferent browser automation approaches consume vastly different context.\n\n\n\nAgent\nOutput Size\nEfficiency\nLink\n\n\n\n\nWebFetch\n~1.5 KB (AI-summarized)\n20x better\nDocs\n\n\nPlaywright MCP\n~10-33 KB (accessibility tree)\nBaseline\nGitHub\n\n\nAgent Browser ⚠️\n~28 KB (accessibility tree)\nProject unmaintained 2026-05 — superseded by browser-use direct mode + Playwright MCP\nGitHub\n\n\nLightpanda\n~16 KB (raw markdown)\n2x better\nGitHub\n\n\n\nFor 10-page workflows: WebFetch = ~15KB vs Playwright = ~330KB total context consumed.\nWhy Accessibility Trees Are Efficient\nThe accessibility tree strips visual styling to retain only semantic structure (name, role, state, value). 10-50x smaller than raw HTML. See: Token cost analysis in browser MCPs.\nFurther Reading\n\nWebFetch vs WebSearch analysis - Deep comparison.\nbrowser-use - Foundation library for AI browser agents.\nChrome full accessibility tree - DevTools feature.\nmcp-compressor - MCP proxy that shows a compressed tool surface first and fetches full schemas on demand, cutting tokens spent on large MCP tool descriptions. \n\nCost Tracking Tools\n\nLangfuse - Open-source LLM observability + cost tracking. offline, no upload. \nOpenLLMetry - OpenTelemetry-based GenAI observability instrumenting LLM and vector-DB calls with per-call token and latency telemetry. \nMLflow - Open-source AI/ML platform with GenAI observability in MLflow 3.x: LLM call tracing with per-span token tracking, prompt optimization tooling, and AI Gateway integration for cost control. \nHelicone AI Gateway - Fastest open-source AI gateway (Rust). \nAnthropic Token Counter - Free pre-flight token counting endpoint.\ntiktoken - OpenAI's fast BPE tokenizer (Python/Rust), 3-6x faster.\nLangSmith Cost Tracking - Automatic recording with dashboards.\nLlamaIndex Cost Analysis - Estimate costs before calls.\n\nPricing Comparison\nLive Pricing Tools\n\nPrice Per Token - Daily-updated, 300+ models.\nArtificial Analysis Calculator - Free calculator, 100+ models.\nArtificial Analysis Leaderboard - Quality + price + speed.\nSimon Willison's LLM Prices - Interactive calculator.\nHelicone LLM Cost Comparison - 300+ model calculator.\nCostGoat - 302+ APIs from 10+ providers.\nLangtail - Side-by-side comparison.\nWhatLLM - 256 models, 43+ providers, weekly updates.\n\nProvider Pricing Pages\n\nAnthropic Pricing - Official Claude model pricing.\nOpenAI Pricing - Official OpenAI API pricing.\nGoogle Gemini Pricing - Official Gemini API pricing.\nDeepSeek Pricing - Official DeepSeek pricing.\nMistral Pricing - Official Mistral pricing.\n\nNotable Recent Pricing (June–July 2026)\n\n\n\nModel\nInput /MTok\nOutput /MTok\nNotes\n\n\n\n\nClaude Fable 5\n$10.00\n$50.00\nAnthropic's most capable model; {"text":"\n\n\n\n\n\n\n2026 in various calendarsGregorian calendar2026MMXXVIAb urbe condita2779Armenian calendar1475ԹՎ ՌՆՀԵAssyrian calendar6776Baháʼí calendar182–183Balinese saka calendar1947–1948Bengali calendar1432–1433Berber calendar2976British Regnal year4 Cha. 3 – 5 Cha. 3Buddhist calendar2570Burmese calendar1388Byzantine calendar7534–7535Chinese calendar乙巳年 (Wood Snake)4723 or 4516    — to —丙午年 (Fire Horse)4724 or 4517Coptic calendar1742–1743Discordian calendar3192Ethiopian calendar2018–2019Hebrew calendar5786–5787Hindu calendars - Vikram Samvat2082–2083 - Shaka Samvat1947–1948 - Kali Yuga5126–5127Holocene calendar12026Igbo calendar1026–1027Iranian calendar1404–1405Islamic calendar1447–1448Japanese calendarReiwa 8(令和８年)Javanese calendar1959–1960Juche calendar115Julian calendarGregorian minus 13 daysKorean calendar4359Minguo calendarROC 115民國115年Nanakshahi calendar558Thai solar calendar2569Tibetan calendarཤིང་མོ་སྦྲུལ་ལོ་(female Wood-Snake)2152 or 1771 or 999    — to —མེ་ཕོ་རྟ་ལོ་(male Fire-Horse)2153 or 1772 or 1000Unix time1767225600 – 1798761599\n2026 (MMXXVI) is the current year, and is a common year starting on Thursday of the Gregorian calendar, the 2026th year of the Common Era (CE) and Anno Domini (AD) designations, the 26th  year of the 3rd millennium and the 21st century, and the  7th   year of the 2020s decade.  \nThe early part of the year saw escalating armed conflicts in the Americas and Middle East. In January, the United States launched a military operation in Venezuela that captured sitting President Nicolás Maduro, leading to a blockade of Venezuelan oil exports that contributed to a crisis in Cuba. In Syria, an offensive by the Syrian government led to the Syrian Democratic Forces eventually being integrated into the Syrian Army, while in Yemen, a counteroffensive by the Yemeni government led to the collapse of the Southern Transitional Council. In February, Pakistan launched airstrikes against Afghanistan, leading to an open war between both nations. In Iran, in response to authorities cracking down on protests, the United States and Israel began a war in late February with the assassination of Supreme Leader Ali Khamenei, which resulted in widespread economic grief, fuel shortages and retaliatory strikes on Gulf nations, as well as the closure of the Strait of Hormuz and a naval blockade, that lasted until June.\n\nThe continued release of the Epstein files that began the previous year has influenced scrutiny, media coverage, and in some cases arrests of high profile individuals in politics, business, and academia in the western world. American businessman Elon Musk became the first person to have a verified net worth exceeding $1 trillion with the initial public offering of his company SpaceX in June. In politics, a conservative wave spread through Latin America, with right-wing victories in Colombia, Costa Rica and Peru while far right parties in Europe continued to gain ground in the United Kingdom and across the European Union, though the long ruling right wing government in Hungary lost power after ruling for 16 years and Portugal elected a centre-left social democrat over a right wing populist in their presidential election.\n\nIn science and technology, the dominant headline so far has been NASA's Artemis II flyby of the Moon, the first crewed flight beyond low Earth orbit since Apollo 17 in 1972, sending the first woman, Black man, and Canadian beyond low Earth orbit. Artificial intelligence has continued to advance, with increasing focus on scaling models, infrastructure, and commercial applications. While some high-profile projects such as OpenAI's Sora were discontinued, development of generative AI—including text-to-video models—has continued across the industry.\n\nIn sports, the 2026 FIFA World Cup became the first edition to be hosted by three nations and the first to include 48 teams and set the record for the highest attendance in World Cup history; the 2026 Winter Olympics were the first Olympic Games to be officially co-hosted by two cities.\n\nIn health, an epidemic of Ebola in the Democratic Republic of the Congo and Uganda has been declared a Public Health Emergency of International Concern by the World Health Organization.\n\n\n\nLa Constellation bar in Crans-Montana, Switzerland, where a fire kills 41 people and injures 116 others on January 1\nMap of the US airstrikes on Venezuela, which resulted in the capture of the Venezuelan president Nicolás Maduro and first lady Cilia Flores on January 3\nProtests take place in Uganda on January 16 due to allegations of fraud over the general election, won by incumbent President Yoweri Museveni\nPrime Minister of Spain Pedro Sánchez and government officials inspecting the Adamuz rail disaster site that people including Jalisco New Generation Cartel leader El Mencho.[61][62]\nFebruary 23 – 2025–2026 Dutch cabinet formation: Rob Jetten is sworn in as Prime Minister of the Netherlands, heading a minority government.[63]\nFebruary 26 – 2026 Afghanistan–Pakistan war: The government of Pakistan declares \"open war\" against the Taliban in Afghanistan.[64]\nFebruary 27 – 2026 Zona da Mata floods: Floods and landslides in the Zona da Mata region of Minas Gerais, Brazil leave at least 70 people dead and thousands of others displaced.[65]\nFebruary 28 – 2026 Iran war: Israel and the United States launch attacks on Iran, killing many high-profile officials, including Supreme Leader Ali Khamenei.[66] Iran launches retaliatory strikes against Israel, as well as against US military bases in the Persian Gulf,[67] and closes the Strait of Hormuz by attacking vessels that try to pass.[68]\n\n\nMojtaba Khamenei becomes the Supreme Leader of Iran on March 8, following his predecessor and father Ali Khamenei's assassination\nMarch 1 – Abiemnom massacre: At least 169 people are killed and 50 injured when armed youth from Unity State attack Abiemnom County in South Sudan.[69]\nMarch 2 – 2026 Lebanon war: Hezbollah begins launching strikes against Israel in retaliation for the assassination of Iranian Supreme Leader Ali Khamenei.[70][71]\nMarch 4 – 2026 Iran war: The United States sinks the Iranian warship IRIS Dena in the Indian Ocean with a torpedo, resulting in 140 sailors missing.[72]\nMarch 5 – 2026 Nepalese general election: The Rastriya Swatantra Party led by Balen Shah wins a landslide victory.[73]\nMarch 5–17 – The 2026 World Baseball Classic is held in Japan and the United States.[74]\nMarch 6–15 – The 2026 Winter Paralympics are held in Milan and Cortina d'Ampezzo, Italy.[75]\nMarch 6–7 – 2026 Kenya floods: At least 66 people are killed after floods across Kenya.[76]\nMarch 8 \n2026 Iranian supreme leader election: Mojtaba Khamenei, the son of Ali Khamenei, is selected as the third Supreme Leader of Iran.[77][78]\n2026 Colombian parliamentary election: President Gustavo Petro's party Historic Pact wins a plurality of seats in the Chamber of Representatives and the Senate.[79]\nIndia beats New Zealand in the 2026 Men's T20 World Cup final and secures its third title.[80]\nMarch 13 \n2026 Iran war: The United States Air Force conducts a large bombing raid on Kharg Island, a key oil export hub off the Persian Gulf coast of Iran.[81]\nFirst Secretary of the Communist Party of Cuba Miguel Díaz-Canel confirms that Cuba is in talks with the Trump administration to find solutions to the oil blockade in the country.[82]\nMarch 15 \n2026 Kazakh constitutional referendum: The new Constitution of Kazakhstan is accepted with 90% in favor.[83]\n2026 North Korean parliamentary election: General Secretary Kim Jong Un's Workers' Party wins a landslide majority in the Supreme People's Assembly.[84][85]\n2026 Vietnamese legislative election: The Communist Party led by General Secretary Tô Lâm wins almost all the seats in the National Assembly.[86]\n2026 Republic of the Congo presidential election: Incumbent President Denis Sassou Nguesso wins reelection in a landslide victory.[87]\nMarch 16 – 2026 Kabul hospital airstrike: At least 400 people are killed and more than 250 injured in Pakistani airstrikes on a hospital in Kabul, Afghanistan.[88]\nMarch 17 – 2026 Iran war: Ali Larijani, the Secretary of the Supreme National Security Council, is assassinated by an Israeli airstrike.[89]\nMarch 20–22 – The 2026 World Athletics Indoor Championships were held at Kujawsko-Pomorska Arena Toruń in Toruń, BiT City, Kuyavian–Pomeranian Voivodeship, Poland.[90][91]\nMarch 22 – 2026 Slovenian parliamentary election: Incumbent Prime Minister Robert Golob wins a plurality of seats in the National Assembly.[92]\nMarch 22–23 – 2026 Italian constitutional referendum: With a higher-than-expected turnout, voters reject a government-backed constitutional reform that would have separated the career paths of judges and prosecutors and split the High Council of the Judiciary into two bodies.[93]\nMarch 23 – A Lockheed C-130 of the Colombian Aerospace Force crashes near Puerto Leguízamo, Colombia, killing 69 people.[94]\nMarch 24\nOpenAI announces that their flagship Sora app and API are shutting down.[95] The app is officially shut down on April 26, and the API's termination is scheduled for September 24.[96]\n2026 Danish general election: Incumbent Prime Minister Mette Frederiksen's coalition loses its majority in the Folketing.[97]\n2026 Iran war: Iran's Ministry of Foreign Affairs addresses in a letter to the United Nations that ships not tied to either the United States or Israel can pass through the Strait of Hormuz.[98]\n\n\nEarthset photo taken on April 6 during Artemis II's lunar flyby\nAftermath of the April 8 Israeli attacks in Beirut, Lebanon\nwhole April: NASA and the European Copernicus Climate Change Service rated April 2026 as the third-warmest April since weather reporting began in 1850.[99]\nApril 1 – NASA launches the Artemis II lunar flyby mission, marking the first crewed flight beyond low Earth orbit since Apollo 17 in 1972.[100]\nApril 6 – The crew of Artemis II breaks the record for the furthest humans have ever been from Earth, reaching a maximum distance of 252,756 miles (406,771 km) as they travel around the far side of the Moon.[101]\nApril 7 \n2026 Vietnamese presidential election: The National Assembly of Vietnam elects General Secretary Tô Lâm as the new president of Vietnam, replacing Lương Cường.[102]\n2026 Iran war: Following an ultimatum from Trump regarding the Strait of Hormuz, the United States and Iran agree on a two-week ceasefire.[103]\nApril 8 – Israel launches a series of airstrikes across Lebanon, targeting Hezbollah infrastructure. More than 300 people are killed and over 1,100 injured.[104]\nApril 10\n2026 Djiboutian presidential election: Incumbent President Ismaïl Omar Guelleh is re-elected for a sixth term.[105]\nThe crew of Artemis II successfully returns to Earth, splashing down safely in the Pacific Ocean near San Diego, California, United States. The four crew members are extracted from the capsule and taken by helicopter to the USS John P. Murtha.[106]\nApril 11 – 2026 Iraqi presidential election: The Iraqi Parliament elects Nizar Amidi of the Patriotic Union of Kurdistan (PUK) as the new President of Iraq, winning with 227 votes in the second round.[107]\nApril 12\n2026 Hungarian parliamentary election: Incumbent Prime Minister Viktor Orbán loses re-election in a landslide to Péter Magyar's Tisza Party, ending 16 years of Fidesz–KDNP rule.[108]\n2026 Beninese presidential election: Independent candidate Romuald Wadagni wins in a landslide with over 94% of the vote.[109]\nApril 13 – 2026 Iran war: A blockade of Iranian ports by the United States takes effect, with President Trump warning that any Iranian vessels attempting to challenge it will be \"immediately eliminated\". Maritime authorities advise ships in the region to expect increased military activity and possible interception procedures.[110]\nApril 16 – 2026 Lebanon war: A US-brokered 10-day ceasefire takes effect between Israel and Lebanon, following ambassador-level talks in the White House.[111]\nApril 19 – 2026 Bulgarian parliamentary election: The Progressive Bulgaria coalition, led by former President Rumen Radev, wins a landslide victory, securing 44% of the vote and an outright majority of seats.[112]\nApril 21 – 2026 Iran war: US President Trump announces a further extension of the ceasefire until an Iranian proposal is submitted and conversations are concluded at the request of Pakistan.[113]\nApril 25 – 2026 Mali offensives: The Azawad Liberation Front and JNIM launch several large-scale attacks, targeting major cities across Mali, capturing Kidal and parts of Gao, Mopti, and Sevare.[114]\n\n\nFirefighters at the scene of the Liuyang fireworks factory explosion that occurred on May 4\nMay 1 – The United Arab Emirates leaves OPEC, ending six decades of membership and removing one of the organization's largest oil producers.[115]\nMay 4\nAn explosion at a fireworks factory in Liuyang, Hunan, China kills 37 people and injures 51 others.[116]\nSudanese civil war: Rapid Support Forces launch drone attacks at several targets in Khartoum, Sudan, including the Khartoum International Airport in Khartoum, Sudan. Drone strikes are also reported at the Signal Corps in Khartoum Bahri and Al-Markhiyat camp in northern Omdurman.[117] Additionally, the Sudan Army's air defenses intercept drone strikes at the airport.[118]\nMay 12 – 2026 Bahamian general election: Incumbent Prime Minister Philip Davis wins a second term in office.[119]\nMay 12–16 – The Eurovision Song Contest 2026 is held in Vienna, Austria, following their win at the Eurovision Song Contest 2025.[120] Bulgarian contestant Dara wins with the song \"Bangaranga\", marking the first time Bulgaria has won the contest.[121]\nMay 15 – Gaza war: An Israeli strike assassinates Izz al-Din al-Haddad, commander of the Izz al-Din al-Qassam Brigades and leader of Hamas in the Gaza Strip.[122]\nMay 16 – 2026 Ituri Province Ebola epidemic: The World Health Organization declares an Ebola outbreak caused by Bundibugyo ebolavirus in the Democratic Republic of the Congo and Uganda a Public Health Emergency of International Concern.[123][124]\nMay 17 – 2026 Cape Verdean parliamentary election: Incumbent Prime Minister Ulisses Correia e Silva loses reelection to PAICV leader Francisco Carvalho.[125]\nMay 20 – Former First Secretary of the Communist Party of Cuba Raúl Castro is indicted by the United States over the 1996 shootdown of Brothers to the Rescue aircraft.[126]\nMay 22\nThe 2026 European heatwaves begin, bringing record-breaking temperatures to several European countries and causing thousands of deaths over the next several weeks.[127]\nA gas explosion at the Liushenyu coal mine in Shanxi, China, kills 82 people.[128]\nMay 24 – 2026 Cypriot legislative election: The Democratic Rally led by Annita Demetriou wins a plurality of seats.[129]\nMay 30 – 2026 Maltese general election: The Labour Party led by incumbent Prime Minister Robert Abela wins their fourth consecutive election.[130]\nMay 31\n2026 Guinean parliamentary election: Parties supporting incumbent President Mamady Doumbouya win the election.[131]\nFlamingo Revolution: Following small protests in the village of Zvërnec, major protests erupt in Albania over a proposed luxury development involving Donald Trump's son-in-law Jared Kushner and his firm Affinity Partners, as well as broader discontent with Prime Minister Edi Rama's government.[132]\n\n\n DSWD personnel inspecting a collapsed commercial building in General Santos following the Mindanao earthquake on June 8\nProtesters in Albania's capital Tirana during the Flamingo Revolution on June 13\nCCTV footage of the moment at which the helicopter involved in the parliamentary election: The Civil Contract, led by incumbent Prime Minister Nikol Pashinyan, wins reelection.[134]\n2026 Kosovan parliamentary election: Amid the ongoing political deadlock, Vetëvendosje, led by incumbent Prime Minister Albin Kurti, wins a plurality of seats.[135][needs update]\n2026 Peruvian general election: Popular Force leader Keiko Fujimori narrowly defeats Together for Peru leader Roberto Sánchez in the presidential runoff. Left-wing parties gain a majority in the Chamber of Deputies but tie in the reestablished Senate.[136]\nJune 8 – A powerful magnitude 7.8 earthquake strikes the Philippines, the strongest in the country since 1976. 82 are killed and 1,319 injured.[137]\nJune 10 – In Barcelona, Spain, the blessing ceremony of the Sagrada Família's tallest tower by Pope Leo XIV is held, exactly 100 years after the death of architect Antoni Gaudí. Pope Leo XIV consecrates and opens the central tower of Jesus Christ.[138] The Sagrada Família is the world's tallest church.[139]\nJune 11 – The National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration declares the onset of an El Niño event in the tropical Pacific, and forecasts a 63% chance that it will rank among the largest since records began in 1950.[140]\nJune 11 – July 19 – The 2026 FIFA World Cup is held in Canada, Mexico, and the United States.[141][needs update]\nJune 12 – Elon Musk becomes the first US dollar trillionaire with the initial public offering of SpaceX.[142]\nJune 12 – July 5 – The 2026 Women's T20 World Cup is held in England and Wales, and is won by Australia.[143]\nJune 13–14 – The 2026 24 Hours of Le Mans is held in Le Mans, France.[144]\nJune 14 – A mid-air collision between two helicopters in Rio de Janeiro, Brazil, kills six people, including American singer-songwriter Oliver Tree, Argentine YouTuber Gaspi, Argentine director and screenwriter Lucas A. Vignale and Brazilian music producer Lucas Frota.[145][146]\nJune 15–17 – The United States and Iran announce and sign the Islamabad Memorandum, a 14-point agreement to end the 2026 Iran war, reopen the Strait of Hormuz, lift the U.S. blockade of Iranian ports, and begin a 60-day negotiation period on Iran's nuclear programme; Israel says it will not withdraw from territory it has seized in southern Lebanon.[147][148]\nJune 21 – 2026 Colombian presidential election: Right-wing outsider Abelardo de la Espriella wins the election in a runoff against left-wing candidate Iván Cepeda.[149]\nJune 22 – Keir Starmer announces his resignation as Prime Minister of the United Kingdom, prompting a leadership election.[150]\nJune 24 – 2026 Venezuela earthquakes: A  7.2 foreshock strikes western Venezuela, followed by a Mw 7.5 mainshock, the strongest in the country since 1900. At least 2,295 people are reported killed, with thousands injured or missing and widespread damage across the country.[151]\n\n\n Ali Khamenei family coffins during their funeral on July 4\nJuly 1 – Members of the Society of Saint Pius X (SSPX) in Écône, Switzerland, consecrate four bishops against the direct orders of Pope Leo XIV, triggering a religious schism between SSPX and the Catholic Church.[152][153][154]\nJuly 2 – The 2026 Algerian parliamentary election is held.[155]\nJuly 4–9 – The state funeral of Ali Khamenei, the Supreme Leader of Iran assassinated during the 2026 Iran war, is held.[156]\nJuly 4–July 18 – The inaugural Nations Championship – Southern Hemisphere Series, an international rugby union tournament, is being held. The Northern Hemisphere Series will take place in November.[157][importance?]\nJuly 6 – Hamas announces the resignation of its civil administration under the Gaza peace plan.[158]\nJuly 7–8 – The 2026 Ankara NATO summit is held in Ankara, Turkey.[159]\nJuly 8 – 2026 Iran war: The Islamabad Memorandum between the United States and Iran breaks down, with U.S. President Trump saying the agreement is \"over\" following renewed U.S. strikes on Iranian targets.[160][161]\n\nPredicted and scheduled events[edit]\nJuly 19 – The 2026 São Toméan presidential election is scheduled to be held.[162]\nJuly {"text":"  ██╗  ██╗███████╗ █████╗ ██████╗ ██████╗  ██████╗  ██████╗ ███╗   ███╗\n  ██║  ██║██╔════╝██╔══██╗██╔══██╗██╔══██╗██╔═══██╗██╔═══██╗████╗ ████║\n  ███████║█████╗  ███████║██║  ██║██████╔╝██║   ██║██║   ██║██╔████╔██║\n  ██╔══██║██╔══╝  ██╔══██║██║  ██║██╔══██╗██║   ██║██║   ██║██║╚██╔╝██║\n  ██║  ██║███████╗██║  ██║██████╔╝██║  ██║╚██████╔╝╚██████╔╝██║ ╚═╝ ██║\n  ╚═╝  ╚═╝╚══════╝╚═╝  ╚═╝╚═════╝ ╚═╝  ╚═╝ ╚═════╝  ╚═════╝ ╚═╝     ╚═╝\n              The context compression layer for AI agents\n\n60–95% fewer tokens (for JSON data), 15-20% fewer tokens (for coding agents) · library · proxy · MCP · content-aware compressors · local-first · reversible\n\n  \n  \n  \n  \n  \n  \n  \n\n\n  Docs ·\n  Install ·\n  Proof ·\n  Agents ·\n  Discord ·\n  llms.txt\n\n\n  AI agents / LLMs: read /llms.txt here, or fetch the live index / full docs blob.\n\n\n\nHeadroom compresses everything your AI agent reads — tool outputs, logs, RAG chunks, files, and conversation history — before it reaches the LLM. Same answers, fraction of the tokens.\n\n  \n  Live: 10,144 → 1,260 tokens — same FATAL found.\n\nWhat it does\n\nLibrary — compress(messages) in Python or TypeScript, inline in any app\nProxy — headroom proxy --port 8787, zero code changes, any language\nAgent wrap — headroom wrap claude|codex|copilot|cursor|aider|opencode|cline|continue|goose|openhands|openclaw|vibe in one command; undo with headroom unwrap <tool>\nMCP server — headroom_compress, headroom_retrieve, headroom_stats for any MCP client\nCross-agent memory — shared store across Claude, Codex, Gemini, auto-dedup\nheadroom learn — mines failed sessions, writes corrections to CLAUDE.local.md (default, gitignored) or CLAUDE.md / AGENTS.md / GEMINI.md\nOutput token reduction — trims what the model writes back (not just what you send): drops ceremony/restated code and skips deep \"thinking\" on routine steps. See Output token reduction.\nReversible (CCR) — originals are cached for retrieval on demand\n\nHow it works (30 seconds)\n Your agent / app\n   (Claude Code, Cursor, Codex, LangChain, Agno, Strands, your own code…)\n        │   prompts · tool outputs · logs · RAG results · files\n        ▼\n    ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n    │  Headroom   (runs locally — your data stays here)  │\n    │  ────────────────────────────────────────────────  │\n    │  CacheAligner  →  ContentRouter  →  CCR            │\n    │                    ├─ SmartCrusher   (JSON)        │\n    │                    ├─ CodeCompressor (AST)         │\n    │                    └─ Kompress-v2-base (text, HF)  │\n    │                                                    │\n    │  Cross-agent memory  ·  headroom learn  ·  MCP     │\n    └────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n        │   compressed prompt  +  retrieval tool\n        ▼\n LLM provider  (Anthropic · OpenAI · Bedrock · …)\n\n\nContentRouter — detects content type, selects the right compressor\nSmartCrusher / CodeCompressor / Kompress-v2-base — compress JSON, AST, or prose\nCacheAligner — stabilizes prefixes so provider KV caches actually hit\nCCR — stores originals locally; LLM calls headroom_retrieve if it needs them\n\n→ Architecture · CCR reversible compression · Kompress-v2-base model card\nGet started (60 seconds)\n# 1 — Install\nuv tool install \"headroom-ai[all]\"      # Install `headroom` CLI as a global tool in self-contained virtual env\npip install \"headroom-ai[all]\"          # Python — ships the `headroom` CLI\nnpm install headroom-ai                 # TypeScript SDK only — no `headroom` CLI\n\n# 2 — Pick your mode  (the `headroom` commands below come from the uv or pip install)\nheadroom wrap claude                    # wrap a coding agent\nheadroom proxy --port 8787              # drop-in proxy, zero code changes\n# or: from headroom import compress      # inline library\n\n# 3 — Verify setup and see the savings\nheadroom doctor                         # health check — confirms routing is working\nheadroom perf\nheadroom dashboard                      # live savings dashboard (proxy must be running)\nTo use headroom, it is recommended you launch a wrapped agent session each time so that all necessary setup is completed. When wrapping a coding agent, headroom starts a local proxy, sets up an MCP server that provides tools such as rtk and tokensave, and launches a coding agent session configured to proxy requests to headroom.\nThe headroom CLI ships only via the PyPI package. The npm headroom-ai is the TypeScript SDK — a library you import (import { compress } from 'headroom-ai'), not a CLI, so it provides no headroom command.\nGranular extras: [proxy], [mcp], [ml], [code], [memory], [vector] (optional HNSW backend — needs a C++ toolchain, not in [all]), [relevance], [image], [agno], [langchain], [evals], [pytorch-mps] (Apple-GPU memory-embedder offload — set HEADROOM_EMBEDDER_RUNTIME=pytorch_mps). Requires Python 3.10+.\nCodex / global install\nIf Codex or another MCP client cannot inherit a shell PATH reliably, install Headroom as a persistent uv tool and point the client at the absolute binary path:\nuv tool install \"headroom-ai[all]\"\ncommand -v headroom\nThen use the returned path in MCP config:\n[mcp_servers.headroom]\ncommand = \"/absolute/path/from/command-v/headroom\"\nargs = [\"mcp\", \"serve\"]\ncommand = \"headroom\" only works when the client starts with a PATH that already includes the uv tool directory.\nProof\nSavings on real agent workloads:\n\n\n\nWorkload\nBefore\nAfter\nSavings\n\n\n\n\nCode search (100 results)\n17,765\n1,408\n92%\n\n\nSRE incident debugging\n65,694\n5,118\n92%\n\n\nGitHub issue triage\n54,174\n14,761\n73%\n\n\nCodebase exploration\n78,502\n41,254\n47%\n\n\n\nAccuracy preserved on standard benchmarks:\n\n\n\nBenchmark\nCategory\nN\nBaseline\nHeadroom\nDelta\n\n\n\n\nGSM8K\nMath\n100\n0.870\n0.870\n±0.000\n\n\nTruthfulQA\nFactual\n100\n0.530\n0.560\n+0.030\n\n\nSQuAD v2\nQA\n100\n—\n97%\n19% compression\n\n\nBFCL\nTools\n100\n—\n97%\n32% compression\n\n\n\nReproduce: python -m headroom.evals suite --tier 1 · Full benchmarks & methodology\nOutput token reduction (cut what the model writes back)\nEverything above shrinks the prompt you send. But you also pay for every\ntoken the model writes back — and on Opus-class models output costs 5× input.\nA lot of that output is waste: \"Great, let me…\" preambles, re-printing code you\njust showed it, and deep \"thinking\" on routine steps like reading a file.\nHeadroom can trim that too, from the proxy, without you changing any code:\n\nVerbosity steering — appends a short \"be terse, don't restate context\"\nnote to the end of the system prompt (so your prompt cache still hits).\nEffort routing — when a turn is just the model resuming after a tool result\n(a file read, a passing test), it dials the model's thinking effort down. New\nquestions and errors keep full effort.\n\nTurn it on:\nexport HEADROOM_OUTPUT_SHAPER=1     # off by default\nheadroom proxy --port 8787\n\nAlready running a proxy? These switches are read live on every request,\nso a proxy that headroom wrap reused (rather than started) would not see\na value you export afterwards — its environment was snapshotted at launch.\nheadroom wrap now hot-syncs your current settings to the running proxy via a\nloopback POST /admin/runtime-env, so they take effect immediately with no\nrestart (no cold start, no dropped requests, no lost caches). Set them before\nyou wrap. On a shared proxy these overrides are global — the last explicit\nsetting wins.\n\nLearn the right terseness for you. People don't say how terse they want\nanswers — they show it (they interrupt long replies, or move on before they\ncould have read them). headroom learn --verbosity reads your past sessions and\npicks the level automatically:\nheadroom learn --verbosity            # preview what it found (dry run)\nheadroom learn --verbosity --apply    # save it; the proxy uses it from now on\nSee how many output tokens you saved. Output savings are counterfactual —\nwe never see what the model would have written — so Headroom reports an honest\nestimate with a confidence range, never a made-up number:\nheadroom output-savings\n# Reduction: 31.7%  (95% CI 27.7% … 35.7%)   [estimated]\nWant a measured number instead of an estimate? Leave 10% of conversations\nunshaped as a control group: export HEADROOM_OUTPUT_HOLDOUT=0.1. The dashboard\nshows an Output Tokens Saved card next to input compression, labelled\nmeasured or estimated with the confidence band.\n→ Full write-up incl. the measurement methodology: Output token reduction\n\n \n   \n \n\nAgent compatibility matrix\n\n\n\nAgent\nheadroom wrap\nNotes\n\n\n\n\nClaude Code\n✅\n--memory · --code-graph · --1m · --tool-search\n\n\nCodex\n✅\nshares memory with Claude\n\n\nCursor\nManual setup\nstarts proxy and prints base URLs for Cursor settings\n\n\nAider\n✅\nstarts proxy + launches\n\n\nCopilot CLI\n✅\nstarts proxy + launches\n\n\nOpenClaw\n✅\ninstalls as ContextEngine plugin\n\n\nOpenCode\n✅\ninjects config · starts proxy + launches\n\n\nCline\n✅\nstarts proxy + injects config\n\n\nContinue\n✅\nstarts proxy + injects config\n\n\nGoose\n✅\nstarts proxy + launches\n\n\nOpenHands\n✅\nstarts proxy + launches\n\n\nMistral Vibe\n✅\nstarts proxy + launches\n\n\nCortex Code\nLibrary only\n60–65% savings (library mode; no wrap)\n\n\n\nAny OpenAI-compatible client works via headroom proxy. MCP-native: headroom mcp install.\nUndo durable wrapping with headroom unwrap <tool> (supports: claude, copilot, codex, opencode, openclaw).\nGitHub Copilot CLI subscription mode\nHeadroom can route GitHub Copilot CLI subscription traffic through the local proxy:\nheadroom copilot-auth login\nheadroom wrap copilot --subscription -- --model gpt-4o\nThis lets Headroom intercept OpenAI-compatible Copilot CLI requests and apply the same proxy compression pipeline before forwarding to GitHub Copilot's hosted API. The wrapper exchanges Headroom's reusable GitHub OAuth token for Copilot's short-lived API token and prints the upstream endpoint as COPILOT_PROVIDER_API_URL=... during launch.\nheadroom copilot-auth login stores a Headroom-specific Copilot OAuth token.\nThis avoids relying on generic GitHub or Copilot CLI tokens that can read\nCopilot account metadata but may still be rejected by Copilot's token-exchange\nendpoint.\nFor GitHub Enterprise Server or custom-domain Copilot deployments, set the\ndeployment domain before launching:\nexport GITHUB_COPILOT_ENTERPRISE_DOMAIN=ghe.example.com\nFor GitHub.com Enterprise Cloud URLs such as\ngithub.com/enterprises/your-enterprise, do not set an enterprise-domain\noverride. Headroom uses GitHub's normal token-exchange endpoint and the Copilot\nAPI endpoint advertised for the signed-in account.\nPlatform support note: macOS auth reuse via Copilot CLI Keychain storage has been smoke-tested. Windows Credential Manager, Linux Secret Service / secret-tool, and Docker/CI token-injection paths are implemented or planned as auth-discovery paths, but still need real OS validation before they should be considered fully vetted. For Docker and CI, prefer passing an explicit GITHUB_COPILOT_TOKEN or GITHUB_COPILOT_GITHUB_TOKEN rather than relying on host keychain access.\nWhen to use · When to skip\nGreat fit if you…\n\nrun AI coding agents daily and want savings without changing your code\nwork across multiple agents and want shared memory\nneed reversible compression — originals are retrievable via CCR within the configured TTL\n\nSkip it if you…\n\nonly use a single provider's native compaction and don't need cross-agent memory\nwork in a sandboxed environment where local processes can't run\n\n\nIntegrations — drop Headroom into any stack\n\n\n\nYour setup\nHook in with\n\n\n\n\nAny Python app\ncompress(messages, model=…)\n\n\nAny TypeScript app\nawait compress(messages, { model })\n\n\nAnthropic / OpenAI SDK\nwithHeadroom(new Anthropic()) · withHeadroom(new OpenAI())\n\n\nVercel AI SDK\nwrapLanguageModel({ model, middleware: headroomMiddleware() })\n\n\nLiteLLM\nlitellm.callbacks = [HeadroomCallback()]\n\n\nLangChain\nHeadroomChatModel(your_llm)\n\n\nAgno\nHeadroomAgnoModel(your_model)\n\n\nStrands\nStrands guide\n\n\nASGI apps\napp.add_middleware(CompressionMiddleware)\n\n\nMulti-agent\nSharedContext().put / .get\n\n\nMCP clients\nheadroom mcp install\n\n\n\n\n\nWhat's inside\n\nSmartCrusher — universal JSON: arrays of dicts, nested objects, mixed types.\nCodeCompressor — AST-aware for Python, JS/TS, Go, Rust, Java, C/C++, Perl.\nKompress-v2-base — our HuggingFace model, trained on agentic traces.\nImage compression — 40–90% reduction via trained ML router.\nCacheAligner — stabilizes prefixes so Anthropic/OpenAI KV caches actually hit.\nLive-zone compression — compresses only new bytes (fresh tool output, latest turn); frozen prefix stays byte-identical so provider cache is not busted. History is never dropped.\nCCR — reversible compression; LLM retrieves originals on demand.\nCross-agent memory — shared store, agent provenance, auto-dedup.\nSharedContext — compressed context passing across multi-agent workflows.\nheadroom learn — plugin-based failure mining for Claude, Codex, Gemini.\n\n\n\nPipeline internals\nHeadroom exposes one stable request lifecycle across compress(), the SDK, and the proxy:\nSetup → Pre-Start → Post-Start → Input Received → Input Cached → Input Routed → Input Compressed → Input Remembered → Pre-Send → Post-Send → Response Received\n\nTransforms do the work: CacheAligner → ContentRouter → SmartCrusher / CodeCompressor / Kompress-base (live-zone only; IntelligentContext and RollingWindow were retired in PR-B1).\nPipeline extensions observe or customize lifecycle stages via on_pipeline_event(...).\nCompression hooks sit alongside the canonical lifecycle as an additional extension seam.\nProxy extensions remain the server/app integration seam for ASGI middleware, routes, and startup policy.\n\nProvider and tool-specific behavior lives under headroom/providers/ so core orchestration stays focused on lifecycle, sequencing, and policy.\n\nCLI/tool slices: headroom/providers/claude, copilot, codex, openclaw\nProvider runtime slices: headroom/providers/claude, gemini, plus shared backend/runtime dispatch in headroom/providers/registry.py\nCore files stay orchestration-first: wrap.py, client.py, cli/proxy.py, and proxy/server.py delegate provider-specific env shaping, API target normalization, backend selection, and transport dispatch.\n\n\nHeadroom for teams\nHeadroom OSS is built for individual developers: run headroom proxy or headroom wrap on your laptop and start cutting tokens in minutes — free, local-first, your data never leaves your machine.\nRunning it across a whole engineering org is a different job: a shared, always-on deployment; centralized config and version rollout; org-wide savings dashboards; SSO and access controls; air-gapped / VPC installs; and someone to call when it matters. That's what we help companies with — self-hosted with support, or fully managed.\nIf your team is spending real money on LLM tokens — Claude Code, Codex, Cursor, or agents running in CI — and you want those savings across everyone, not just one laptop:\n→ Email hello@headroomlabs.ai with your stack and rough monthly LLM spend, and we'll help you roll Headroom out across your organization.\nEverything in this repo stays open source (Apache 2.0). The managed offering is simply for teams that would rather have it deployed, supported, and scaled for them.\nInstall\npip install \"headroom-ai[all]\"          # Python, everything — includes the `headroom` CLI\nnpm install headroom-ai                 # TypeScript SDK (library only — no `headroom` CLI)\ndocker pull ghcr.io/chopratejas/headroom:latest\nGranular extras: [proxy], [mcp], [ml] (Kompress-v2-base), [code], [memory], [vector] (optional HNSW backend — needs a C++ toolchain, not in [all]), [relevance], [image], [agno], [langchain], [evals], [pytorch-mps] (Apple-GPU memory-embedder offload — set HEADROOM_EMBEDDER_RUNTIME=pytorch_mps). Requires Python 3.10+.\n\nNote: [all] covers the core stack but excludes framework adapters. Install them separately: pip install \"headroom-ai[langchain]\" (also [agno], [strands], [anyllm], [bedrock]).\n\nUsing pipx? Choose a supported interpreter explicitly:\npipx install --python python3.13 \"headroom-ai[all]\"\n\nPick 3.13 if you want dollar savings. The dashboard's Proxy $ Saved tile prices compression with LiteLLM, and LiteLLM can't be installed on Python 3.14+. On 3.14 token savings still track, but the dollar figure stays $0.00. If you already installed on 3.14, switch with pipx reinstall headroom-ai --python python3.13 and restart the proxy.\n\n→ Installation guide — Docker tags, persistent service, PowerShell, devcontainers.\n\nCPU requirement (x86/x86_64): the ONNX-backed features — Magika content\ndetection and embedding relevance — use a precompiled ONNX Runtime that needs\nAVX2. On x86 hosts without AVX2 (some Docker/QEMU setups and older cloud\nVMs) Headroom automatically falls back to its non-ONNX paths (BM25 relevance,\nheuristic detection) rather than crashing. arm64/Apple Silicon needs no AVX2.\n\nUpdating\nheadroom update          # detects pip / pipx / uv tool and upgrades in place\nheadroom update --check  # report the latest release without upgrading\nheadroom update --pre    # include pre-releases\nheadroom update figures out how Headroom was installed (pip/venv, pip --user,\npipx, uv tool) and runs the matching upgrade across macOS, Linux, and Windows.\nFor git checkouts, editable installs, Docker images, and externally-managed\nsystem Pythons (PEP 668) it prints the correct manual step instead of guessing.\nThe proxy also shows a one-line \"update available\" notice on startup. It checks\nPyPI at most once a day, in the background, and never blocks. Opt out with\nHEADROOM_UPDATE_CHECK=off (also skipped in --stateless mode and CI).\nCorporate / SSL-inspection environments\nIf pip install \"headroom-ai[all]\" fails with CERTIFICATE_VERIFY_FAILED\n(unable to get local issuer certificate), your network uses SSL inspection — a MITM\nproxy presenting a company-issued CA. The build backend (maturin) downloads rustup over a\nconnection your TLS stack doesn't trust. Install Rust first so the build doesn't fetch it:\n# macOS / Linux\ncurl --proto '=https' --tlsv1.2 -sSf https://sh.rustup.rs | sh && rustup default stable\n# Windows\nwinget install Rustlang.Rustup && rustup default stable\nRestart your shell, then pip install \"headroom-ai[all]\". A prebuilt wheel avoids the Rust\nbuild entirely where available: pip install --only-binary headroom-ai headroom-ai. Prebuilt\nwheels are published for Windows (win_amd64), Linux (x86_64 / aarch64), and macOS\n(Apple Silicon and Intel), so installs on those platforms never need a local Rust toolchain — the\nRust-first dance above is only for the platform-independent sdist fallback when no wheel matches.\nTwo runtime assets are fetched over TLS; if they are blocked, trust your corporate CA via\nREQUESTS_CA_BUNDLE / SSL_CERT_FILE / CURL_CA_BUNDLE:\n\ncdn.pyke.io — the ONNX Runtime for the Rust core. Alternatively pre-provide it with\nORT_STRATEGY=system and ORT_LIB_LOCATION=/path/to/onnxruntime.\nhuggingface.co — the kompress-base compression model. Pre-download it and run with\nHF_HUB_OFFLINE=1, or set HF_ENDPOINT to a trusted mirror.\n\nRunning with compression disabled (pure gateway) requires neither asset.\n\"Basic Constraints of CA cert not marked critical\" (Python 3.13+ strict mode)\nA different failure from the one above. If TLS fails with:\n[SSL: CERTIFICATE_VERIFY_FAILED] certificate verify failed:\nBasic Constraints of CA cert not marked critical\n\nthen the corporate CA is found and trusted — adding it to a CA bundle changes nothing.\nPython 3.13 + OpenSSL 3.x enable VERIFY_X509_STRICT by default, which enforces RFC 5280\n§4.2.1.9: a CA cert's basicConstraints must be marked critical. Inspection roots like\nZscaler set CA:TRUE without the critical bit, so the chain is rejected.\nSet HEADROOM_TLS_STRICT=0 to clear only the strict flag from every TLS context\nHeadroom controls — the proxy's httpx upstream client and the urllib3/huggingface_hub\npath used for model downloads. Chain validation, signature, expiry, and hostname checks all\nstay on; this is strictly narrower than disabling verification.\nHEADROOM_TLS_STRICT=0 headroom proxy --port 8787\nThe Rust core's ONNX download (cdn.pyke.io) uses a separate TLS stack (rustls / OS trust\nstore), unaffected by HEADROOM_TLS_STRICT. On Windows the corporate root must be in the\nmachine certificate store (browsers already trust it there); or pre-provision ONNX\nRuntime with ORT_STRATEGY=system + ORT_LIB_LOCATION=/path/to/onnxruntime to skip the\ndownload entirely.\nheadroom learn\n\n  \n\nheadroom learn — mines failed sessions, writes corrections to CLAUDE.local.md (default, gitignored; use --target CLAUDE.md for the shared team file) / AGENTS.md / GEMINI.md.\nDocumentation\n\n\n\nStart here\nGo deeper\n\n\n\n\nQuickstart\nArchitecture\n\n\nProxy\nHow compression works\n\n\nMCP tools\nCCR — reversible compression\n\n\nMemory\nCache optimization\n\n\nFailure learning\nBenchmarks\n\n\nConfiguration\nLimitations\n\n\nPersistent installs (headroom init / headroom install apply)\nSavings analytics (headroom savings / headroom perf / headroom doctor)\n\n\n\nCompared to\nHeadroom runs locally, covers every content type, works with every major framework, and is reversible.\n\n\n\n\nScope\nDeploy\nLocal\nReversible\n\n\n\n\nHeadroom\nAll context — tools, RAG, logs, files, history\nProxy · library · middleware · MCP\nYes\nYes\n\n\nRTK\nCLI command outputs\nCLI wrapper\nYes\nNo\n\n\nlean-ctx\nTool output, files, shell, history\nProxy · library · middleware · MCP · CLI\nYes\nYes\n\n\nCompresr, Token Co.\nText sent to their API\nHosted API call\nNo\nNo\n\n\nOpenAI Compaction\nConversation history\nProvider-native\nNo\nNo\n\n\n\n\nAttribution.
